      <a href="/user/show/1719023-kelly" class="user" title="Kelly">Kelly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/14962.Where_or_When" title="Paperback 9780156031271" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer39083274">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7306165107322682315">I have to put this one in the 'Hated it' category. It's truly one of the most terrible books I've ever read with the most selfish characters imaginable. It's about a couple who reunites after only knowing each other after meeting in a summer camp when they were 12. Supposedly, they "fell in love", but their continued love story which knows no bounds, not even the bonds of marriage, and is less about love and more about lust. You'll find more smut than the worst Harlequinn novel between the pages</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7306165107322682315">I have to put this one in the 'Hated it' category. It's truly one of the most terrible books I've ever read with the most selfish characters imaginable. It's about a couple who reunites after only knowing each other after meeting in a summer camp when they were 12. Supposedly, they "fell in love", but their continued love story which knows no bounds, not even the bonds of marriage, and is less about love and more about lust. You'll find more smut than the worst Harlequinn novel between the pages and not much more substance. Some of the smutty lines were SO awful, I read them to a friend who told me to stay out of the 99¢ paperback romances. It's basically a recognization, a meeting, a very disgusting affair, one of those "this will never work" epiphanies and then the book goes to crap from there. Just about every book by Anita Shreve revolves around people having affairs, and THIS is undoubtedly the worst of them all.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_101962445">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101962445" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1383849-patrick" class="left imgcol" title="Patrick"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1226811925p2/1383849.jpg" alt="Patrick" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/101962445?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 12, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1383849-patrick" class="user" title="Patrick">Patrick</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14962.Where_or_When" title="Paperback 9780156031271" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer101962445">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12864223627496887448">I love this book because it interposes the akward innocence of deep young love with the carnality of mature love. The book is summed up in this quote: "Was there, or could there ever be, he wondered then, and wonders now, a reconciliation between innocence and sexuality?" It does this by intertwining present day sex sessions with flashbacks to the intensity of young adolescent love in which every gesture and touch meant something. <br /><br />The book is about old innocent first lovers who meet again 31 yea</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12864223627496887448">I love this book because it interposes the akward innocence of deep young love with the carnality of mature love. The book is summed up in this quote: "Was there, or could there ever be, he wondered then, and wonders now, a reconciliation between innocence and sexuality?" It does this by intertwining present day sex sessions with flashbacks to the intensity of young adolescent love in which every gesture and touch meant something. <br /><br />The book is about old innocent first lovers who meet again 31 years later. It is interesting because they seem to have been soul mates as kids. From their correspondence, they seem to have depth and an inquisitive nature that is not present in their lives with their respective spouse. In other words, they connect on a deeper level which I believe is a laudible goal. I think the unfaithfulness in their respective marriage comes from the fact that not only are they each others first loves but also they are tempermentally similar so they understand each other implicitly. Life with their current spouses seem to exist because of similar day-to-day experiences instead of a deeper connection with each other. <br /><br />Furthermore, I think infidelity in a marriage always start with seeds of discontent in ones relationship. The biggest seed of discontent in the book and marriage in general is financial. Without an external stressor such as finance, I think one can have contented marriage though not necessarily a happy one. <br /><br />This leads me to believe one has to choose ones spouse very carefully. Why not have both, a person that you connect with in depth and cement that with being with each other in your day-to-day experiences?<br /><br />I think this book is great because it explores the fine line between being in love and lusting after someone. I personally think being in love, lusting, and loving someone is a continuum that is not easily definable and I think the book shows this conitnuum. It is clear that these two adults are in love because of the obssessive thinking that occurs between both people, the illogical behavior that they do, the constant remembering of the past and the withdrawal symptoms of love when the person is not with their beloved. But it seems to me that once they started physically touching each other their mental/emotional love has turned into lust. <br /><br />So is it really being in love or lust? I think in their case it is being in love because it starts out with something mental/emotional toward the other person instead of their body parts (physcial attraction that usually occurs when one is lusting overs someone).<br /><br />I think the ending of the book is perfect because it exentuates the love found and lost of their teenage years. <br /><br />I also like the fact that it shows the real consequences to other people because of the infidelity that occurs. <br /><br />So far this leads me to a few conclusions about a successful marriage. A successful marriage has to start out with the spouses understanding the essence of the other and from that shared understanding create a life with shared goals that both are passionate about. Secondly, the couple must set a side time to rekindle the relationship separate from day-to-day worries. In other words, a periodic vacation to reconnect with each others essence and not worry about day-to-day affairs. Thirdly, it is vitally important to not allow any festering problems in the marriage that can cause a riff that can possibly lead to infidelity due to a mental/emotional disconnect. I think that takes is honest communication with each other.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12864223627496887448">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/1859396-lisa" class="left imgcol" title="Lisa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1231010168p2/1859396.jpg" alt="Lisa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/706038182?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 28, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1859396-lisa" class="user" title="Lisa">Lisa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14962.Where_or_When" title="Paperback 9780156031271" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer706038182">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13176426758252328109">Ok, first, they were 14, not 12. If you don't believe a person can fall in love at 14, don't bother reading this, or "Romeo and Juliet," either. Second, some of the sex scenes were graphic, but it was not "smutty" and nothing like a Harlequin novel. Anita Shreve is a gifted writer, regardless of whether you personally like her characters. Third, who reads fiction for moral guidance? It's a novel, about fictional--and flawed--characters, not a self-help book. <br /><br />I found the descriptions of the chara</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13176426758252328109">Ok, first, they were 14, not 12. If you don't believe a person can fall in love at 14, don't bother reading this, or "Romeo and Juliet," either. Second, some of the sex scenes were graphic, but it was not "smutty" and nothing like a Harlequin novel. Anita Shreve is a gifted writer, regardless of whether you personally like her characters. Third, who reads fiction for moral guidance? It's a novel, about fictional--and flawed--characters, not a self-help book. <br /><br />I found the descriptions of the characters' emotions compelling, but I must admit I'm really annoyed at the way the book ended. Was that a Catholic thing, that they had to atone for their sins? (I'm Catholic, so that's not an insult to Catholics.). I think I would have preferred an ending that left things more uncertain. </span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/689749067" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/19018822-susan-espourteille" class="left imgcol" title="Susan Espourteille"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1373561666p2/19018822.jpg" alt="Susan Espourteille" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/689749067?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 08, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/19018822-susan-espourteille" class="user" title="Susan Espourteille">Susan Espourteille</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14962.Where_or_When" title="Paperback 9780156031271" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer689749067">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2548113982259001752"> I have to say I am shocked by all the negative reviews of this book. I found it phenomenal, a tour de force of love, lust, destiny and confusion. I saw the ending coming almost from the very beginning, yet I was compelled to read on, compelled to find out how they reached the inevitable train wreck.<br /><br /> I'm not sure why many people dislike books simply because they dislike, or cannot relate to the characters. Many masterpieces of literature have despicable characters; the story and its denouement a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2548113982259001752"> I have to say I am shocked by all the negative reviews of this book. I found it phenomenal, a tour de force of love, lust, destiny and confusion. I saw the ending coming almost from the very beginning, yet I was compelled to read on, compelled to find out how they reached the inevitable train wreck.<br /><br /> I'm not sure why many people dislike books simply because they dislike, or cannot relate to the characters. Many masterpieces of literature have despicable characters; the story and its denouement are the factors which sway me. If I dismissed every book that had a character I disliked, I'd have few books to recommend.<br /><br /> I disagree with those who call the protagonists selfish. They are both in loveless, cold marriages; their respective spouses could be seen as selfish and self-absorbed as well. What married person has not looked back on a previous live with the 20-20 vision of hindsight, asking themselves, "What if. . . ?"<br /><br /> I found this to be a compelling and masterful look at love and marriage through the lens of time. I think it is indeed possible to be complacently married, and blindsided by the past; indeed, I think most of us are only a few steps away from the brink of an all-consuming vortex of longing and regret.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2548113982259001752">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/301768-judith" class="left imgcol" title="Judith"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1387898807p2/301768.jpg" alt="Judith" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/547313656?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 26, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/301768-judith" class="user" title="Judith">Judith</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14962.Where_or_When" title="Paperback 9780156031271" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer547313656">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3100021855365494609">I have so many conflicting feelings about this book that I really hesitate to presume to write a review. In the first place: this is such a childish plot, it's more like a Nicholas Sparks book. Two people meet 30 years after they fell in love at camp and spent only one week together when they were age 14. Who does that in real life?!<br /><br />In the second place, this book is really an anachronism because so much of the communication is based on desperate letters sent by overnight mail and phone calls mad</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3100021855365494609">I have so many conflicting feelings about this book that I really hesitate to presume to write a review. In the first place: this is such a childish plot, it's more like a Nicholas Sparks book. Two people meet 30 years after they fell in love at camp and spent only one week together when they were age 14. Who does that in real life?!<br /><br />In the second place, this book is really an anachronism because so much of the communication is based on desperate letters sent by overnight mail and phone calls made from phone booths. I kept thinking how different the story might be if they had cell phones and face book and email. Yet it is not set in the distant past, just the recent past. So it gave me such an odd feeling, like I had lived through time travel somehow. <br /><br />Thirdly, I really hate and despise people who neglect or ignore their children because they are blinded by passion. I can't forgive them or find their romance romantic. I only find it selfish and despicable. <br /><br />But finally, this book was so disturbing that I found it hard to sleep the night I finished it, and though I<br /> kept thinking of all the reasons I didn't like it, I had to admit it was powerful. So, when a book can move your emotions and thoughts that much, you have to give credit where credit is due, regardless of whether you " like" it or not. Bravo, Anita Shreve. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3100021855365494609">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_319583880">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/319583880" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8083434-mirvan-ereon" class="left imgcol" title="Mirvan  Ereon"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1340334159p2/8083434.jpg" alt="Mirvan  Ereon" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/319583880?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 26, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8083434-mirvan-ereon" class="user" title="Mirvan  Ereon">Mirvan  Ereon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14962.Where_or_When" title="Paperback 9780156031271" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8083434-mirvan-ereon?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8083434-mirvan-ereon?shelf=excellent-ideas" class="actionLinkLite">excellent-ideas</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8083434-mirvan-ereon?shelf=reread-again-in-the-future" class="actionLinkLite">reread-again-in-the-future</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer319583880">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1714269281582363185">Despite what other people said, I really liked this book. it was well-written and the story was very intriguing. Young love, coming-of-age, reunion and infidelity, things I love to read in a novel every day. Besides, this book is so dear in my heart for it discusses first love, losing it and then finding it back again after years of waiting and almost forgetting that there was still a person out there who still remembers you. Maybe this book gave me some hope that this could also happen to me. W</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1714269281582363185">Despite what other people said, I really liked this book. it was well-written and the story was very intriguing. Young love, coming-of-age, reunion and infidelity, things I love to read in a novel every day. Besides, this book is so dear in my heart for it discusses first love, losing it and then finding it back again after years of waiting and almost forgetting that there was still a person out there who still remembers you. Maybe this book gave me some hope that this could also happen to me. Well, if it happens in book, why not in real life, right? Books are almost always based on real life, so maybe, where or when, I might still have a chance to have this kind of beautiful story - poignant and unforgettable.<br /><br />I will definitely reread this again to savor the bittersweet swirls of emotion it gave me.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1714269281582363185">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/1551908-bill" class="user" title="Bill">Bill</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer523387082">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18331561991996042121">The author presents a very graphic portrayal of that common query “What might have been?” of two people grasping with a gap of 31 years since first meeting as young teenagers. Their dilemma is in balancing erotic love with morality and responsibility, both having relatively normal but not completely satisfying marriages and children they adore, but with both marriages besought with what seem like relatively trivial personal issues, but very serious financial problems. <br /><br />The very enlightening narra</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18331561991996042121">The author presents a very graphic portrayal of that common query “What might have been?” of two people grasping with a gap of 31 years since first meeting as young teenagers. Their dilemma is in balancing erotic love with morality and responsibility, both having relatively normal but not completely satisfying marriages and children they adore, but with both marriages besought with what seem like relatively trivial personal issues, but very serious financial problems. <br /><br />The very enlightening narrative covers many human aspects of the reunion with its romantic overtones, unbridled passion and obsession bordering on addiction. However, the realities of life and mind numbing questions of guilt, betrayal and pending financial ruin intrude with a vengeance.<br /><br />Like myself, some readers may relate to specific issues, which cover a vast range of thoughts and actions, in what is a fairly common phenomenon in today’s society.<br /><br />I found the book to be mind absorbing with a very moving ending and recommend it as a good soul searching read.<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer445954808">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18190932295452334369">The sad thing about this book is that it is not believable at all. And it's not in the fantasy genre, so no excuses. I'm a romantic to the core, but I highly doubt that these two very immatured people found love at the age of 14, and that too in a week's time. Uh huh, I'm not buying that! More like lust, if you ask me. <br /><br />Charles comes across to me as an irresponsible, deranged man who just wants to escape from his financial troubles. Also, it's quite amazing how he is broke, but he magically alway</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18190932295452334369">The sad thing about this book is that it is not believable at all. And it's not in the fantasy genre, so no excuses. I'm a romantic to the core, but I highly doubt that these two very immatured people found love at the age of 14, and that too in a week's time. Uh huh, I'm not buying that! More like lust, if you ask me. <br /><br />Charles comes across to me as an irresponsible, deranged man who just wants to escape from his financial troubles. Also, it's quite amazing how he is broke, but he magically always has enough money to make calls to Sian and book a hotel room for their rendezvous. I wish I could say something nice about Sian; those brief moments when she appeared to change her mind, I actually wanted to applaud her. But oh, you fickle-minded woman! <br /><br />The only saving grace was the ending. A classic lesson of why being selfish never pays. Would I recommend this book? No, unless someone is interested in cringing through pages of a repulsive plot, and all the time having murderous intentions towards the main characters. Sad, really. <br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3165898630628658934">I normally enjoy reading books by Anita Shreve, however, this book was nothing like her other books in not only the style of which it was written but also it's contexts.<br /><br />Where or When is about 2 people who met at camp when they were in their late teens. They fell in love during that week and then they both went on to live their seperate lives. Fast forward 31 years and they meet again, fall back in love and start an illicit affair - both are married with children. <br /><br />I had great difficulty reading t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3165898630628658934">I normally enjoy reading books by Anita Shreve, however, this book was nothing like her other books in not only the style of which it was written but also it's contexts.<br /><br />Where or When is about 2 people who met at camp when they were in their late teens. They fell in love during that week and then they both went on to live their seperate lives. Fast forward 31 years and they meet again, fall back in love and start an illicit affair - both are married with children. <br /><br />I had great difficulty reading this book. Having my own family, it's hard to read about a man who has an affair and is ready to leave his family to start his life with his new love. I didn't mind so much that he would leave his wife, but what bothered me is that he didn't think twice about his 3 kids (all under 10) he would leave behind. WOW!!<br /><br />I would not recommend this book. It was not a pleasure read for me and unfortunately, I try not to not finish a book. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer192714575">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2680811576957330433">I haven't read anything by Anita Shreve before. Not sure if this was written for a predominantly female or male readership, but as a guy I found sufficient depth, sensitivity, and insight into the middle aged male psyche here to send shivers down my spine. Published in the early nineties, the subtext of the story is one of financial decline, depression, businesses closing,... therefore every bit as relevant now in 2011 as it was back then.<br /><br />The male and female leads here are middle aged, both marr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2680811576957330433">I haven't read anything by Anita Shreve before. Not sure if this was written for a predominantly female or male readership, but as a guy I found sufficient depth, sensitivity, and insight into the middle aged male psyche here to send shivers down my spine. Published in the early nineties, the subtext of the story is one of financial decline, depression, businesses closing,... therefore every bit as relevant now in 2011 as it was back then.<br /><br />The male and female leads here are middle aged, both married to other people, both unfulfilled. They have an affair. I thought it was beautifully done, but personally I didn't like the ending - can't say more without spoiling it, but surely, there had to be another way? <br /><br />Anyway, a powerful story. I'll definitely look out for other titles by Anita Shreve. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2680811576957330433">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer8075357505233796199">Guess I'm not a hopeless romantic. This book was a little too sappy for me. To me, the love of your life is the one with whom you weather all of life's storms and sunny days, not the person to whom you were physically attracted during one week of your childhood. Total destruction and devastation were the result of the betrayal and selfishness that came from chasing a dream that was probably too good to be true in the long haul. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5157033748389168154">This is the second Anita Shreve book I have read and I found it very similar to the other (The Last Time They Met). Both had middle-aged people reuniting with their one true love from their youth. Both had dramatic endings - though this one did not match the astonishing ending of The Last Time They Met. And both I found to be faintly wishy-washy in the first part, an almost dreamlike quality appearing in the writing with lots of atmospheric language. The second half picked up and went hurtling t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5157033748389168154">This is the second Anita Shreve book I have read and I found it very similar to the other (The Last Time They Met). Both had middle-aged people reuniting with their one true love from their youth. Both had dramatic endings - though this one did not match the astonishing ending of The Last Time They Met. And both I found to be faintly wishy-washy in the first part, an almost dreamlike quality appearing in the writing with lots of atmospheric language. The second half picked up and went hurtling towards the conclusion and I found that I really wanted to carry on reading. But ultimately I was left unsatisfied - I didn't find the characters believable - especially as children. (If they had really been so drawn to each other and had such a passionate snog on their last night of camp, would they really have sneaked off the next morning ..... and played badminton!!!!. I think I have other Anita Shreve books on my To Read shelf - I don't think I'll rush to them but will probably give her another try at some point.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer663279074">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5232924268859695792">A picture in a news advertisement; the "innocent" exchange of a few letters; an aranged meeting after 31 years, and lives are changed forever. Where or When is one of those disturbing stories that some of us have magically lived, some of us have longingly wished for, and some of us are grateful to have never experienced. Throughout, readers ride on a wave of emotions that range from heart-wrenching sympathy to sensual excitement to overwhelming disgust. It's a story that deeply loves, breaks hea</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5232924268859695792">A picture in a news advertisement; the "innocent" exchange of a few letters; an aranged meeting after 31 years, and lives are changed forever. Where or When is one of those disturbing stories that some of us have magically lived, some of us have longingly wished for, and some of us are grateful to have never experienced. Throughout, readers ride on a wave of emotions that range from heart-wrenching sympathy to sensual excitement to overwhelming disgust. It's a story that deeply loves, breaks hearts, and ends lives all in one. <br /><br />Anita Shreve, as always, writes with beautiful tone and command of character. She pulls you in, plays on your sympathies, and before you know it, you are rooting for things you know in your moral conscience are wrong. You grieve for chances lost and for hearts maimed by the unfairness of a life that deals in things that can never be changed or redone. <br /><br />In the book, nobody wins. And it is exceedingly fitting.<br /><br />Casey Hays<br />Author of <a title="The Cadence by Casey Hays" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16086196.The_Cadence">The Cadence</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5232924268859695792">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_355788069">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/355788069" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10486977-themadhatter" class="left imgcol" title="TheMadHatter"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1340681071p2/10486977.jpg" alt="TheMadHatter" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/355788069?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 25, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10486977-themadhatter" class="user" title="TheMadHatter">TheMadHatter</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14962.Where_or_When" title="Paperback 9780156031271" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/10486977-themadhatter?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10486977-themadhatter?shelf=adult" class="actionLinkLite">adult</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10486977-themadhatter?shelf=real-life" class="actionLinkLite">real-life</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer355788069">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15674470057509019242">I expected not to like this book (given the adulterous subject matter) but I actually enjoyed it and felt the reality of the situation in the writing. Ms Shreve has a writing style that I love reading and she has such a way of creating characters that are so real in their flaws and thoughts that you feel that this is not a work of fiction. She adds different media into her story either through adding newspaper articles and research papers (which she did in strange fits of passion) and letters be</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15674470057509019242">I expected not to like this book (given the adulterous subject matter) but I actually enjoyed it and felt the reality of the situation in the writing. Ms Shreve has a writing style that I love reading and she has such a way of creating characters that are so real in their flaws and thoughts that you feel that this is not a work of fiction. She adds different media into her story either through adding newspaper articles and research papers (which she did in strange fits of passion) and letters between the two main characters (in this book). Her endings are always surprising and not at all predictable.</span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1369056167?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 20, 2015</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/14962.Where_or_When" title="Paperback 9780156031271" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/25326846-mary-karpel-jergic?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1369056167">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3762096550488841285">I like Shreve's writings about loss and longing and relationships. Its funny, after reading other readers' reviews, I would not describe this as a romantic novel. I thought it was more about getting older and facing up to the life that you have made. Lives can feel empty. They become mundane, we take things for granted and a long term relationship suffers alongside all our personal longings and sense of loss.<br /><br />I also think that it captures the fantasy that's inherent in any extra-marital relations</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3762096550488841285">I like Shreve's writings about loss and longing and relationships. Its funny, after reading other readers' reviews, I would not describe this as a romantic novel. I thought it was more about getting older and facing up to the life that you have made. Lives can feel empty. They become mundane, we take things for granted and a long term relationship suffers alongside all our personal longings and sense of loss.<br /><br />I also think that it captures the fantasy that's inherent in any extra-marital relationship. It is not what really happened that matters, it's what the people think that happened that fills the head and feeds the longings. An event becomes embellished, exaggerated and foolishly placed upon a pedestal.<br /><br />Every character here had some dissatisfaction with life. A sense of something missing and as often happens the grass can look so much greener on the other side. The irony is, grass grows where it is watered. A long standing marriage with cracks needs attention but instead adultery offers an immediate and exciting route away. However it is seldom thought through as in this novel and what we see is the way that adultery breaks people. Nobody is prepared for the guilt, "the tremulous drag of guilt, a line snagged with seaweed."<br /><br />Life can never be the same. "I am in disgrace now. Removed from a state of grace."</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3762096550488841285">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1268311876">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1268311876" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8241787-mary-hawley" class="left imgcol" title="Mary Hawley"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442470678p2/8241787.jpg" alt="Mary Hawley" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1268311876?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 30, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8241787-mary-hawley" class="user" title="Mary Hawley">Mary Hawley</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14962.Where_or_When" title="Paperback 9780156031271" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1268311876">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4435260731693097281">I would give this book four stars for the writing and no stars for the man at the center of it, Charles Callahan, so I've compromised with two. I can buy a teen romance that is rekindled years later, and I get how hard times and failed hopes can lead faithful partners to stray, but Charles Callahan annoys me to no end: his business is collapsing and he does nothing to keep it going or come up with another plan; he hasn't bothered telling his wife that their home will be foreclosed on right after</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4435260731693097281">I would give this book four stars for the writing and no stars for the man at the center of it, Charles Callahan, so I've compromised with two. I can buy a teen romance that is rekindled years later, and I get how hard times and failed hopes can lead faithful partners to stray, but Charles Callahan annoys me to no end: his business is collapsing and he does nothing to keep it going or come up with another plan; he hasn't bothered telling his wife that their home will be foreclosed on right after Christmas; he has no sense of his three children as individuals but loves them collectively, sort of, when he can be bothered; he drinks all day and lives in his own little bubble of denial. SO. When he sees a photo in the paper of his teenage love and drops everything he's not doing to obsessively pursue her, and she is enthralled by him because she, too, is still in the spell of that long-ago love, I can only believe she would have to notice pretty fast that he is pathetically immature and self-absorbed. Instead she finds it sweet when he refuses to look at her photos ("It hurts that this is you, and I wasn't there," says the big baby) and overlooks many other signs that her old flame is wacko. All of this is told in lovely, poetic prose that kept me reading even though I wanted to ditch Charles before the ink dried on his next sappy love letter. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4435260731693097281">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/35653080-diana-woodham" class="user" title="Diana Woodham">Diana Woodham</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1157118184">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12806625314690106155">(*spoiler) Ok.... this book from the start didn't grab my attention. I felt it very hard to get into the book until at least half way through. Neither of the characters in this book are likeable. I realize this is a fictional novel but I found the story line to be completely unrealistic. I had an entirely different picture in my head about what this book was to be about (I don't read the backs of books because I want to have my own opinion about what the book is about) but I had the gist of what</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12806625314690106155">(*spoiler) Ok.... this book from the start didn't grab my attention. I felt it very hard to get into the book until at least half way through. Neither of the characters in this book are likeable. I realize this is a fictional novel but I found the story line to be completely unrealistic. I had an entirely different picture in my head about what this book was to be about (I don't read the backs of books because I want to have my own opinion about what the book is about) but I had the gist of what the book was going to be about. Having said that, I think if the characters in this book hadn't been 14, but a few years older, and their "relationship" didn't only last for one week at a camp then the story would have been more believable and probably a lot more interesting. The fact that they both left their husband/wife and children after 30+ years of not seeing each other and only knowing each other after a week at camp... It would just never happen. In fact, if I got a letter from someone I had only known for a week I'd think they were a serious creeper haha. The ending I felt was thrown together and didn't make a whole lot of sense too. Wasn't a "bad" book, but wasn't a great one. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12806625314690106155">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1038897085">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1038897085" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2645276-jules" class="left imgcol" title="Jules"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Jules" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1038897085?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 28, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2645276-jules" class="user" title="Jules">Jules</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/893809.Where_or_When" title="Paperback 9780349105857" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2645276-jules?shelf=modern-day-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">modern-day-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2645276-jules?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2645276-jules?shelf=contemporary-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2645276-jules?shelf=american-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">american-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2645276-jules?shelf=beach-reading" class="actionLinkLite">beach-reading</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2645276-jules?shelf=romantique" class="actionLinkLite">romantique</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1038897085">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5367987040018013399">I have very mixed feelings about this book and although it is contemporary fiction (a genre that I love) there was a little too much romance between the pages to realistically make it a book of real significance to me personally.<br /><br />This could give the impression that I am a bit of a hard nut and un-romantic but this is not so. Instead, I like all books to have a deal of realism about them and I’m not sure that this one did. Confusingly and despite these comments, something about the book drew me in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5367987040018013399">I have very mixed feelings about this book and although it is contemporary fiction (a genre that I love) there was a little too much romance between the pages to realistically make it a book of real significance to me personally.<br /><br />This could give the impression that I am a bit of a hard nut and un-romantic but this is not so. Instead, I like all books to have a deal of realism about them and I’m not sure that this one did. Confusingly and despite these comments, something about the book drew me in although I experienced limitations in my enjoyment.<br /><br />For me, both the male and female protagonists seemed a bit too tied down by the stereotypes of love and being in love and, at times, they became, for me, a bit too carried away with their romantic feelings meaning that the metaphor of their actual romance became a bit naff (as we say in the UK) and the sex scenes were a little over exaggerated to the degree where they overlapped into highly comical. Basically, at various points during the reading I found myself thinking ‘are real couples and real people actually like this when emotional and sexual feelings are at stake’? Although I really like Shreve’s writing, I also think these several lapses into the comical often tainted the dialogue between the characters. Would you really expect your partner, lover or friend to say (either in writing or orally) ‘the two of us together, down by the lake – it seemed that we were both reality and metaphor at once for something I barely understand’? No, it’s never happened to me either!<br /><br />The whole hypothesis of this tale is to ask is to ask if your first love can be your true love. It also ponders on the whole generic nature of love and the difference between ‘love’ and ‘romantic love’ – well, we all know there is one, right? <br /><br />Generally, I think that over the reading experience I could cope with the plot and hypothesis, it was the characters however that really irked me. Within them, I found very little balance and scale. They played the ‘textbook sexual romance’ like the ‘textbook sexual romance’ giving way to nothing except eventual disaster. What can I say? The guy here gets to play ‘the guy’ and the female is allowed to display some sexual, feminine charm. Families will be wronged. Children will suffer. I guess this is another counterfeit American dream that Shreve is able to produce only too well. Statutory, average, branded -that kind of thing. Kind of like McDonalds but in writing – everybody knows it’s a bit wrong but the damn thing is still in business and many people will continue to partake on a regular basis. Maybe I should have just ordered a regular fries with this? Let’s say it sufficed as a read within itself but it was far from the scale of a filet mignon book – the overall taste and quality were simply not up to scratch.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5367987040018013399">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Jack T. Oliver has a solid marriage, a cozy house in Corpus Christi, and a job he loves as a driver for the Great Western Trailways bus line. In a few weeks, Jack is going to be promoted to Master Operator in recognition of his years of perfect service and on-time driving. It\'s a good life. Until a White Widow boards his bus, on a one-way ticket from Victoria to Corpus Christi. A White Widow is a wild card, a woman traveling alone who can change the course of a driver\'s life, and not always for the best. What happens when Jack Oliver\'s White Widow passes through his life is as unforgettable as it is irrevocable. Within weeks, without ever even learning her name, he will fall passionately in love—and lose everything he has, a few things he never had, and some he never thought about until they were gone.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"2775164710514845030\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent($(this));; return false;\"&gt;...more&lt;\/a&gt;\n\n    &lt;\/div&gt;\n\n      &lt;div class=\'wtrButtonContainer wtrSignedOut\' id=\'8_book_41261\'&gt;\n&lt;div class=\'wtrUp wtrLeft\'&gt;\n&lt;form action=\"/shelf/add_to_shelf\" accept-charset=\"UTF-8\" method=\"post\"&gt;&lt;input Since an assignment in Cape Town ended in tragedy and regret, Nadine has not returned to South Africa, or opened her heart–until she hears the story of Jason Irving. Jason, an American student, was beaten to death by angry local youths at the height of the apartheid era. Years later, his mother is told that Jason’s killers have applied for amnesty. Jason’s parents pack their bags and fly from Nantucket to Cape Town. Filled with rage, Jason’s mother resolves to fight the murderers’ pleas for forgiveness.As Nadine follows the Irvings to beautiful, ghost-filled South Africa, she is flooded with memories of a time when the pull toward adventure and intrigue left her with a broken heart. Haunted by guilt and a sense of remorse, and hoping to lose herself in her coverage of the murder trial, Nadine grows closer to Jason’s mother as well as to the mother of one of Jason’s killers–with profound consequences. In a country both foreign and familiar, Nadine is forced to face long-buried demons, come to terms with the missing pieces of her own family past, and learn what it means to truly love and to forgive.With her dazzling prose and resonant themes, Amanda Eyre Ward has joined the ranks of such beloved American novelists as Anne Tyler and Ann Patchett. Her children are grown and gone, her husband is more married to his job than to her, and now they\'re about to pack up once more. Panicked at the thought of having to start all over again, Joanna commits the first irresponsible act of her life. She runs away to Pawleys Island, South Carolina, a place she\'s been to just once. She finds a job as a live-in companion to Grace Finelli, a widow who has come to the island to fulfill a girlhood dream. Together the two women embark on the most difficult journey of their lives: Joanna struggling for independence, roots, and a future of her own, as her family tugs at her from afar; and Grace, choosing to live the remainder of her life for herself alone, knowing she may never see her children again. Entwined is Paul Harrison\'s story as he loses his wife, his job, and everything that defines him as a man. He takes off on his own journey out west, searching for the answers to all that has gone wrong in his life. One thing remains constant: He wants his wife back. Joanna, however, is moving farther away from her old life as she joins a group dedicated to rescuing endangered loggerhead turtles, led by a charismatic fisherman unlike anyone she\'s ever met. The Richest Season is a stunning debut about three very different people, each changing their lives when such transformations are usually long over.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3530.Anita_Shreve">About Anita Shreve</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/3530.Anita_Shreve"><img alt="3530" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1239738864p2/3530.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer897782143832319331">Anita Shreve grew up in Dedham, Massachusetts (just outside Boston), the eldest of three daughters. Early literary influences include having read Ethan Frome by Edith Wharton when she was a junior in high school (a short novel she still claims as one of her favorites) and everything Eugene O'Neill ever wrote while she was a senior (to which she attributes a somewhat dark streak in her own work). A</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText897782143832319331">Anita Shreve grew up in Dedham, Massachusetts (just outside Boston), the eldest of three daughters. Early literary influences include having read Ethan Frome by Edith Wharton when she was a junior in high school (a short novel she still claims as one of her favorites) and everything Eugene O'Neill ever wrote while she was a senior (to which she attributes a somewhat dark streak in her own work). After graduating from Tufts University, she taught high school for a number of years in and around Boston. In the middle of her last year, she quit (something that, as a parent, she finds appalling now) to start writing. "I had this panicky sensation that it was now or never."<br /><br />Joking that she could wallpaper her bathroom with rejections from magazines for her short stories ("I really could have," she says), she published her early work in literary journals. One of these stories, "Past the Island, Drifting," won an O. Henry prize. Despite this accolade, she quickly learned that one couldn't make a living writing short fiction. Switching to journalism, Shreve traveled to Nairobi, Kenya, where she lived for three years, working as a journalist for an African magazine. One of her novels, The Last Time They Met, contains bits and pieces from her time in Africa.<br /><br />Returning to the United States, Shreve was a writer and editor for a number of magazines in New York. Later, when she began her family, she turned to freelancing, publishing in the New York Times Magazine, New York magazine and dozens of others. In 1989, she published her first novel, Eden Close. Since then she has written 12 other novels, among them The Weight of Water, The Pilot's Wife, The Last Time They Met, A Wedding in December, and Body Surfing.<br /><br />In 1998, Shreve received the PEN/L. L. Winship Award and the New England Book Award for fiction. In 1999, she received a phone call from Oprah Winfrey, and The Pilot's Wife became the 25th selection of Oprah's Book Club and an international bestseller. In April 2002, CBS aired the film version of The Pilot's Wife, starring Christine Lahti, and in fall 2002, The Weight of Water, starring Elizabeth Hurley and Sean Penn, was released in movie theaters. <br /><br />Still in love with the novel form, Shreve writes only in that genre. "The best analogy I can give to describe writing for me is daydreaming," she says. "A certain amount of craft is brought to bear, but the experience feels very dreamlike."<br /><br />Shreve is married to a man she met when she was 13. She has two children and three stepchildren, and in the last eight years has made tuition payments to seven colleges and universities.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="897782143832319331">...more</a>

    </div>
